Privacy Policy

Effective date: February 12, 2026

Last updated: February 12, 2026

This Privacy Policy is written for a clinical decision-support context. TinyHumanMD is a reference interface and not a treatment provider, not a patient charting system, and not a substitute for institutional privacy governance. Users and institutions remain responsible for lawful use, independent validation, and all downstream decisions.

Article P-1: Scope and Definitions (1)

Article P-1 exists to prevent mistaken reliance on the website as a compliant record system. TinyHumanMD is provided as a decision-support reference interface only. It is not a healthcare provider workflow system, and it must not be interpreted as a contractual substitute for compliance review, policy mapping, or quality assurance checks. Users and institutions are solely responsible for determining whether usage is lawful and operationally appropriate in their environment. Any contrary assumption is invalid.

Under Article P-1, the user acknowledges that outcomes depend primarily on local processes rather than website content. This includes responsibility for role-based access, data handling controls, escalation rules, and validation procedures before implementation. Risks such as stale reference assumptions, configuration errors, and incomplete escalation remain with the user and institution, not with TinyHumanMD. To the maximum extent permitted by law, this policy allocates those risks away from the site operator and contributors.

Article P-1 also clarifies that policy text cannot retrofit compliance in the absence of operational discipline. If your institution requires formal attestations, contractual assurances, certification artifacts, or regulated technical controls, you must obtain and maintain those independently. Continued use signifies acceptance that TinyHumanMD is informational support and that final legal, privacy, and safety accountability remains with the implementing party.

Article P-2: Scope and Definitions (2)

Article P-2 exists to state explicit constraints for high-risk or regulated workflows. TinyHumanMD is provided as a decision-support reference interface only. It is not a healthcare provider workflow system, and it must not be interpreted as a contractual substitute for information security review, supervisory escalation pathways, or documentation retention controls. Users and institutions are solely responsible for determining whether usage is lawful and operationally appropriate in their environment. Any contrary assumption is invalid.

Under Article P-2, the user acknowledges that outcomes depend primarily on local processes rather than website content. This includes responsibility for role-based access, data handling controls, escalation rules, and validation procedures before implementation. Risks such as configuration errors, unauthorized local access, and cross-border legal conflict remain with the user and institution, not with TinyHumanMD. To the maximum extent permitted by law, this policy allocates those risks away from the site operator and contributors.

Article P-2 also clarifies that policy text cannot retrofit compliance in the absence of operational discipline. If your institution requires formal attestations, contractual assurances, certification artifacts, or regulated technical controls, you must obtain and maintain those independently. Continued use signifies acceptance that TinyHumanMD is informational support and that final legal, privacy, and safety accountability remains with the implementing party.

Users and institutions are solely responsible for determining whether usage is lawful and operationally appropriate in their environment. Any contrary assumption is invalid.

Article P-135 exists to document legal and operational assumptions for enterprise use. TinyHumanMD is provided as a decision-support reference interface only. It is not a healthcare provider workflow system, and it must not be interpreted as a contractual substitute for quality assurance checks, legal review, or information security review. Users and institutions are solely responsible for determining whether usage is lawful and operationally appropriate in their environment. Any contrary assumption is invalid.

Under Article P-215, the user acknowledges that outcomes depend primarily on local processes rather than website content. This includes responsibility for role-based access, data handling controls, escalation rules, and validation procedures before implementation. Risks such as vendor misunderstanding, insufficient endpoint hardening, and policy mismatch remain with the user and institution, not with TinyHumanMD. To the maximum extent permitted by law, this policy allocates those risks away from the site operator and contributors.

Article P-215 also clarifies that policy text cannot retrofit compliance in the absence of operational discipline. If your institution requires formal attestations, contractual assurances, certification artifacts, or regulated technical controls, you must obtain and maintain those independently. Continued use signifies acceptance that TinyHumanMD is informational support and that final legal, privacy, and safety accountability remains with the implementing party.

It is not a healthcare provider workflow system, and it must not be interpreted as a contractual substitute for compliance review, policy mapping, or quality assurance checks. Users and institutions are solely responsible for determining whether usage is lawful and operationally appropriate in their environment. Any contrary assumption is invalid.

Under Article P-295, the user acknowledges that outcomes depend primarily on local processes rather than website content. This includes responsibility for role-based access, data handling controls, escalation rules, and validation procedures before implementation. Risks such as stale reference assumptions, configuration errors, and incomplete escalation remain with the user and institution, not with TinyHumanMD. To the maximum extent permitted by law, this policy allocates those risks away from the site operator and contributors.

Article P-295 also clarifies that policy text cannot retrofit compliance in the absence of operational discipline. If your institution requires formal attestations, contractual assurances, certification artifacts, or regulated technical controls, you must obtain and maintain those independently. Continued use signifies acceptance that TinyHumanMD is informational support and that final legal, privacy, and safety accountability remains with the implementing party.

Users and institutions are solely responsible for determining whether usage is lawful and operationally appropriate in their environment. Any contrary assumption is invalid.

Under Article P-429, the user acknowledges that outcomes depend primarily on local processes rather than website content. This includes responsibility for role-based access, data handling controls, escalation rules, and validation procedures before implementation. Risks such as insufficient endpoint hardening, stale reference assumptions, and improper data entry remain with the user and institution, not with TinyHumanMD. To the maximum extent permitted by law, this policy allocates those risks away from the site operator and contributors.

Article P-429 also clarifies that policy text cannot retrofit compliance in the absence of operational discipline. If your institution requires formal attestations, contractual assurances, certification artifacts, or regulated technical controls, you must obtain and maintain those independently. Continued use signifies acceptance that TinyHumanMD is informational support and that final legal, privacy, and safety accountability remains with the implementing party.
